## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: nonlinear oscillations / classical mechanics
**Analysis**: This task models the acceleration (dv_dt) of a nonlinear harmonic oscillator as a function of position x, velocity v, and time t. The acceleration typically arises from nonlinear restoring forces, damping terms, and possibly external driving forces.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Simple harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (linear restoring force)
- Damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear restoring + linear damping)
- Duffing oscillator (undriven): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Damped Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (cubic restoring + damping)
- Driven damped Duffing: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (with periodic driving)
- Quadratic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * v (asymmetric restoring force)
- Van der Pol type: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * (1 - c2 * x**2) * v (nonlinear damping)
- Pendulum-like: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * x) (sinusoidal restoring force)
- Damped pendulum driven: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * x) + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (driven damped pendulum)
- Quintic Duffing: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 + c3 * v (higher-order nonlinearity)
- Nonlinear damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * abs(v) (quadratic velocity damping)
- Mixed nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x * v**2 (position-velocity coupling)
- Driven with quadratic and cubic: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 + c3 * v + c4 * cos(c5 * t)
- Mathieu-type parametric: dv_dt = (c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x + c3 * v (parametrically driven)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x**3, x**5) indicate symmetric potential wells (Duffing-type systems)
- Even-power terms in position (x**2) indicate broken symmetry / asymmetric potential wells
- Velocity-dependent terms proportional to (1 - c*x**2)*v suggest self-sustained oscillations (limit cycles, Van der Pol type)
- Sinusoidal functions of position sin(c*x) indicate angular/pendulum-type restoring forces rather than polynomial springs
- Periodic functions of time cos(c*t) or sin(c*t) indicate external harmonic driving forces
- Products x*v or x**2*v indicate nonlinear coupling between position and velocity (energy-dependent damping)
- Time-dependent coefficients multiplying x suggest parametric excitation (Mathieu/Floquet systems)
- Negative linear coefficient on x combined with positive cubic coefficient indicates a double-well potential (bistability)
- Cubic velocity terms v**3 indicate higher-order nonlinear dissipation mechanisms
- Absence of explicit time dependence suggests an autonomous system where energy is conserved or monotonically dissipated
